    <div class = "article" id="titleStoryLine">

rel="login">Edit</a>
    </span>
    
        <h2>Storyline</h2>
        
        <div class="inline canwrap">
            <p>
                <span>    American Grit is a physical, military-based reality competition, hosted by wrestling superstar John Cena. 16 American contestants are divided into four teams of four, which are all lead by four separate American military service people. The four team leaders/coaches consist of an Army Ranger sniper, a Navy Seal team leader, a Marine Corps sergeant, and an Army sergeant - all of whom have seen combat, and all of whom are highly decorated. The contestants will have to fight through challenge after challenge, all of which are modeled after real military training platforms, while dealing with the elements of the wilderness - not to mention each other. At the end of each episode, the team leaders of the 3 losing teams will pick a contestant from their team to run the dreaded Circus obstacle course. The obstacle course stays the same throughout the competition, but the "endurance challenge" at the end of the Circus changes from week to week. A contestant cannot be voted or kicked out of ...</span>
                <em class="nobr">Written by
<a href="/search/title?plot_author=brandon%20hutson&view=simple&sort=alpha&ref_=tt_stry_pl"
>brandon hutson</a></em>            </p>
        </div>

        <h2>Did You Know?</h2>
    <div id="trivia" class="txt-block">
        <h4>Trivia</h4>
    Noah Galloway lost his left arm and left leg after his vehicle tripped an IED while he was stationed in Iraq. With the use of prosthetics, he went on to compete on Dancing With The Stars during its 20th season. He was paired with Sharna Burgess and they came in 3rd place.        <a href="trivia?ref_=tt_trv_trv"

    <div class="article" id="titleUserReviewsTeaser">
        <h2>User Reviews</h2>
        <div class="user-comments">
                    <div class="tinystarbar" title="6/10">
                        <div style="width: 60px;">&nbsp;</div>
                    </div>
                <span>
                    <strong>Go back to Season One!!!</strong>
                    <div class="comment-meta">
                        5 July 2017 | by <a href="/user/ur69964651/?ref_=tt_urv"
><span>lilac-31582</span></a>
                        &ndash; <a href="/user/ur69964651/comments?ref_=tt_urv"
>See all my reviews</a>
                    </div>
                    <div>
                        <p>Season 1=10/10, Season 2=3/10. Season 1 had it all, physical challenges, cadres with killer backgrounds, and obstacles courses that had to be completed before the final challenge had to be completed! It made sense. Now, it&#39;s too much reality. These women Marines are so emotional (not that they shouldn&#39;t be), and the 2 cadre men are typical I guess. One is supposed to be a drill Sargent but half the stuff he says for motivating his crazy emotional team is flat out dumb. You have a high school reject looking to be popular or have a redo in life, another girl on the same team cries every episode (literally). Another chick, does her makeup every episode &amp; could give 2 you-know-what&#39;s about the competition &amp; on top of it, her boobs couldn&#39;t be more present in every episode as well. Season 1 was about athletic challenges and about the contestants, now it&#39;s just about the reality and helping people from people who have serious problems themselves. To be honest, these cadres look like they were the rejects in their respective branches. Im sure even John Cena is like &quot;what the heck did I sign up for with this season?&quot; FOX- please go back to the original premise of the show with real contestants, real cadres, and real hardcore challenges that show American GRIT!</p>
                    </div>
                </span>
